
## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Migration Guide: Envoy External Processing Filter (v1.30 → v1.31)

## Task

Generate a comprehensive migration guide for upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 to version 1.31.0**.

## Context

The workspace contains two versions of the Envoy codebase:
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.30/` - Envoy v1.30.0 (April 2024)
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.31/` - Envoy v1.31.0 (July 2024)

## Scope

Focus specifically on the **External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter** configuration and implementation changes. This filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses.

Your migration guide should identify and document:

1. **Breaking Changes** - Incompatible configuration or behavioral changes
2. **Deprecated Features** - Fields or modes marked for future removal
3. **New Features** - Added capabilities and configuration options
4. **Configuration Updates** - Required or recommended changes to ext_proc filter configuration
5. **Behavioral Changes** - Modifications to filter behavior or runtime semantics

## Relevant Components

The ext_proc filter is primarily located in:
- Proto definitions: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/`
- Implementation: `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/`
- Documentation: `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`

## Deliverable

Write your migration guide to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format with the following sections:

1. **Overview** - Summary of the migration and major changes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Critical incompatible changes requiring action
3. **Deprecated Features** - Features marked for deprecation with migration advice
4. **New Features** - New capabilities and how to use them
5. **Migration Steps** - Step-by-step instructions for upgrading configurations
6. **Testing Recommendations** - How to validate the migration
7. **Rollback Guidance** - How to revert if issues occur

## Requirements

- Provide specific proto field names and types
- Include before/after configuration examples for each breaking change
- Explain the motivation or benefit behind major changes
- Cite specific source files where implementations changed
- Recommend best practices for adopting new features
- Identify common migration pitfalls or edge cases

## Tips

- Compare the two version directories to identify changed proto fields and implementation files
- Search for all API modifications in the ext_proc filter
- Trace configuration usage patterns across both versions
- Look for related documentation updates

Perfect! I've successfully generated a comprehensive migration guide for the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter upgrade from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0. 

## Summary of Changes Documented

The migration guide covers:

### **Breaking Changes (Section 2)**
- **Route Cache Handling Redesign:** Transition from boolean `disable_clear_route_cache` to the new `route_cache_action` enum with three explicit states: DEFAULT, CLEAR, and RETAIN
- Detailed before/after configuration examples
- Behavior comparison table

### **Deprecated Features (Section 3)**
- `disable_clear_route_cache` marked for migration
- Clear deprecation timeline

### **New Features (Section 4)**
1. **route_cache_action enum** - Explicit control over route caching with three options
2. **deferred_close_timeout** - Controls stream closure timing in observability mode (default 5 seconds)
3. **Enhanced Error Handling** - Timeout errors now correctly return `504 Gateway Timeout` instead of `500 Internal Server Error`

### **Key Migration Content**
- **Configuration Updates** - Step-by-step migration path with examples
- **Behavioral Changes** - Detailed explanation of what changed and why
- **Migration Steps** - 6-phase deployment procedure
- **Testing Recommendations** - Unit tests, integration tests, load tests
- **Rollback Guidance** - Quick recovery procedures
- **Common Patterns** - 4 real-world migration scenarios
- **Compatibility Matrix** - Feature support across versions

The guide is comprehensive, includes specific proto field locations, provides concrete configuration examples, and is structured for easy reference during upgrades.

The documentation is now available at `/workspace/documentation.md`.

After the initial\\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n44: // and how it should be processed.\\n45: //\\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n47: //\\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n53: //\\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\\n57: //\\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n63: //   to SEND.\\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n69: //   request trailers.\\n70: //\\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n74: // from the external processor. (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n25: // External Processing Filter\\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n27: \\n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n29: \\n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n32: //\\n33: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n34: \\n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n37: //\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n42: //\\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n45: // and how it should be processed.\\n46: //\\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n48: //\\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n54: //\\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\\n58: //\\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n64: //   to SEND.\\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n70: //   request trailers.\\n71: //\\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n82: //\\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n90: //\\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n92: // server\\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n96: //\\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n99: // name.\\n100: //\\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n110: \\n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n112:     // the external processor response.\\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\\n114: \\n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n116:     // the external processor response. In this case, Envoy will eventually timeout the external processor stream according to this time limit.\\n264:   // The default value is 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if not specified.\\n265:   google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\\n266: }\\n267: \\n268: // The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\\n269: // dynamic metadata. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\\n290:   // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\\n291:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\\n292: }\\n293: \\n294: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\\n295: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\\n296: //\\n297: // This works as below:\\n298: //\\n299: //   1.     "content": "1: syntax = \"proto3\";\n2: \n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n4: \n5: import \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\n6: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n7: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\n8: import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n9: import \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n10: \n11: import \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\n12: import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n13: \n14: import \"udpa/annotations/migrate.proto\";\n15: import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n16: import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n17: \n18: option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\n19: option java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\n21: option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n23: \n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n25: // External Processing Filter\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n27: \n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n29: \n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n32: //\n33: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n34: \n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n37: //\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n42: //\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n45: // and how it should be processed.\n46: //\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n48: //\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n54: //\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\n58: //\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n64: //   to SEND.\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n70: //   request trailers.\n71: //\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n79: //\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n82: //\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n90: //\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n92: // server\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n96: //\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n99: // name.\n100: //\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\n110: \n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n112:     // the external processor response.\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\n114: \n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n118:     // to true.\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\n120:   }\n121: \n122:   reserved 4;\n123: \n124:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n125: \n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n127:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n129: \n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n132:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n133:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n134:   // downstream client will be reset.\n135:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n136:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n137:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n138: \n139:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n140:   // sent. The metadata\n200:   // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n201:   // ext_proc filter name.\n202:   google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n203: \n204:   // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n205:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n206:   // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n207:   // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n208:   // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n209:   bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n210: \n211:   // If set to true, ignore the\n212:   // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n213:   // message in an external processor response. This behavior can be reverted by setting runtime guard\n94:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.udp_socket_apply_aggregated_read_limit`` to ``false``.\n95: - area: statistics\n96:   change: |\n97:     Hot restart statistics like ``hot_restart_epoch`` are only set when hot restart is enabled.\n98: - area: dns\n99:   change: |\n100:     Changes the behavior of the ``getaddrinfo`` DNS resolver so that it treats ``EAI_NODATA`` and ``EAI_NONAME``\n101:     as successful queries with empty results, instead of as DNS failures. This change brings the\n102:     ``getaddrinfo`` behavior in-line with the c-ares resolver behavior. This behavior can be reverted by\n103:     setting the runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.dns_nodata_noname_is_success`` to ``false``.\n104: - area: access_log\n105:   change: |\n106:     The upstream connection address, rather than the upstream host address, will be used for the ``%UPSTREAM_REMOTE_ADDRESS%``,\n107:     ``%UPSTREAM_REMOTE_PORT%`` and ``%UPSTREAM_REMOTE_ADDRESS_WITHOUT_PORT%`` access log format specifiers.\n108:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard\n109:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.upstream_remote_address_use_connection`` to ``false``.\n110: - area: access_log\n111:   change: |\n112:     The ``%CEL%`` formatter supports call functions.\n113: - area: http\n114:   change: |\n115:     Changing header validation checks in the substitution format utility and CEL code to do RFC-compliant header validation.\n116:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.consistent_header_validation`` to ``false``.\n117: - area: quic\n118:   change: |\n119:     Cache source/destination address instances in a LRU cache for packet read to improve performance.\n120:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard\n121:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.quic_upstream_socket_use_address_cache_for_read`` to ``false``.\n122: - area: quic\n123:   change: |\n124:     When a quic connection socket is created, the socket's detected transport protocol will be set to ``quic``.\n125: - area: config\n126:   change: |\n127:     In xDS configuration, the :ref:`AUTO <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.core.v3.ApiVersion.AUTO>` value now means\n128:     :ref:`V3 <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.core.v3.ApiVersion.V3>`. :ref:`AUTO <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.core.v3.ApiVersion.AUTO>`\n129:     is the default value of the enum, so this field may be omitted from all configurations now.\n130: - area: filters\n131:   change: |\n132:     Set ``WWW-Authenticate`` header for ``401`` responses from the Basic Auth filter.\n133: - area: jwt_authn\n134:   change: |\n135:     jwt_authn now validates provider URIs. If the validation is too strict it can temporarily be\n136:     disabled by setting the runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.jwt_authn_validate_uri`` to\n137:     ``false``.\n138: - area: http\n139:   change: |\n140:     Removed runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.refresh_rtt_after_request`` and legacy code path.\n141: - area: http\n142:   change: |\n143:     Changing HTTP/2 semi-colon prefixed headers to being sanitized by Envoy code rather than nghttp2. Should be a functional no-op but\n144:     guarded by ``envoy.reloadable_features.sanitize_http2_headers_without_nghttp2``.\n145: - area: http\n146:   change: |\n147:     Envoy will now proxy ``104`` headers from upstream, though as with ``100`` only the first 1xx response\n148:     headers will be sent. ``104`` headers are designated by IETF's draft-ietf-httpbis-resumable-upload RFC.\n149:     This behavioral can be temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard\n150:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.proxy_104`` to ``false``.\n151: - area: jwt_authn\n152:   change: |\n153:     Changes the behavior of the\n154:     :ref:`forward <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.jwt_authn.v3.JwtProvider.forward>`\n155:     config. Previously, the config only removes JWT if set in headers. With this addition, the config can also be\n156:     used to remove JWT set in query parameters. This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard\n157:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.jwt_authn_remove_jwt_from_query_params`` to ``false``.\n158: - area: custom response filter\n159:   change: |\n160:     Prevent the redirect policy from sending ``100`` as the overridden response code as the custom response must\n161:     be complete.\n162: - area: http\n163:   change: |\n164:     Reject messages with chunked transfer encoding with chunk extension containing ``CR`` not followed by ``LF``. This can be\n165:     temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.http1_balsa_disallow_lone_cr_in_chunk_extension``\n166:     to ``false``.\n167: - area: quic\n168:   change: |\n169:     A change in QUICHE has renamed all flags formerly of the form ``quic_reloadable_flag_...`` to ``quiche_reloadable_flag_...``.\n170:     Likewise, for ``quic_restart_flag_...``, now ``quiche_restart_flag_...``. Consequently, all Envoy flags of those forms with an\n171:     ``envoy_quic_...`` prefix have been similarly renamed to ``envoy_quiche_...``.\n172: - area: hashing\n173:   change: |\n174:     Change murmurHash2 hashing on big endian platforms to generate the same values as little endian platforms.\n175: - area: gcp_authn\n176:   change: |\n177:     Use the fixed URL format instead of one from the configuration. This behavior can be disabled by setting runtime flag\n178:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.gcp_authn_use_fixed_url`` to false.\n179: \n180: bug_fixes:\n181: - area: admission control\n182:   change: |\n183:     Fixed the thread-local controller's average RPS calculation to be calculated over the full\n184:     lookback window. Previously, the controller would calculate the average RPS over the amount of\n185:     time elapsed since the oldest valid request sample. {
  "content": "# Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) Filter Migration Guide\n## v1.30.0 \u2192 v1.31.0\n\n**Release Date:** July 19, 2024\n\n---\n\n## 1. Overview\n\nThis migration guide covers the upgrade path for the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from version 1.30.0 (April 2024) to version 1.31.0 (July 2024). The ext_proc filter enables external services to intercept and process HTTP traffic through a bidirectional gRPC stream.\n\nThe v1.31.0 release introduces several significant improvements to the ext_proc filter, including better control over route cache handling, enhanced error reporting, support for deferred stream closure in observability mode, and improved gRPC context propagation for tracing.\n\n**Key Headlines:**\n- New `route_cache_action` enum provides explicit control over route caching behavior\n- Timeout errors now return `504 Gateway Timeout` instead of `500 Internal Server Error`\n- Support for deferred stream closure timeout in observability mode\n- Enhanced tracing context propagation in gRPC bidirectional streams\n- Deprecation of `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean in favor of the new enum\n\n---\n\n## 2. Breaking Changes\n\n### 2.1 Route Cache Handling Redesign\n\n**Impact Level:** \u26a0\ufe0f **Moderate** - Requires configuration review and potential behavioral changes\n\nThe route cache clearing mechanism has been redesigned to use an explicit enum-based approach instead of a simple boolean flag.\n\n#### What Changed\n\n**v1.30.0 Configuration:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Boolean flag to disable route cache clearing\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n}\n```\n\n**v1.31.0 Configuration:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Enum-based route cache action (RECOMMENDED)\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    DEFAULT = 0;   // Clear only if ext_proc says so\n    CLEAR = 1;     // Always clear\n    RETAIN = 2;    // Never clear\n  }\n\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18;\n\n  // Legacy boolean (still supported but marked for migration)\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Path\n\n**If you are currently using `disable_clear_route_cache: true`:**\n```yaml\n# v1.30.0 Configuration\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Route cache is never cleared\n```\n\n**Upgrade to v1.31.0:**\n```yaml\n# v1.31.0 Configuration (RECOMMENDED)\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**If you are currently using the default behavior (`disable_clear_route_cache` not set):**\n```yaml\n# v1.30.0 Configuration (implicit DEFAULT behavior)\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    # disable_clear_route_cache not set means: clear on ext_proc request\n```\n\n**Upgrade to v1.31.0:**\n```yaml\n# v1.31.0 Configuration (RECOMMENDED)\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Clear only if ext_proc response says so\n```\n\n#### Behavior Comparison Table\n\n| Scenario | v1.30.0 Config | v1.31.0 Equivalent | Behavior |\n|----------|-----------------|-------------------|----------|\n| Default route cache handling | (not set) | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Clear cache based on ext_proc response |\n| Never clear route cache | `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Never clear cache |\n| Always clear route cache | (not supported) | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | **NEW:** Always clear cache regardless of ext_proc response |\n\n#### Implementation Details\n\n- **Source File:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto` (lines 103-120)\n- **Proto Field:** `RouteCacheAction` enum with three values: DEFAULT (0), CLEAR (1), RETAIN (2)\n- **Deprecation Timeline:** The `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean will remain functional in v1.31.0 and subsequent releases, but using `route_cache_action` is strongly recommended\n\n#### Why This Change\n\nThe new enum-based approach provides three explicit states:\n1. **DEFAULT (0):** Follows ext_proc response directives - better for dynamic decision-making\n2. **CLEAR (1):** Always clears cache - useful for routes that require fresh decisions\n3. **RETAIN (2):** Never clears cache - useful for read-only operations or performance-sensitive paths\n\nThis is more explicit than the boolean approach and eliminates ambiguity around default behavior.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Deprecated Features\n\n### 3.1 `disable_clear_route_cache` Boolean Field\n\n**Status:** Deprecated (still functional in v1.31.0)\n\n**Deprecation Message:** Use `route_cache_action` enum instead\n\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field is marked with UDPA deprecation annotation `field_migrate.oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"`, indicating it will eventually migrate to a oneof grouping.\n\n**Migration Advice:**\n1. Replace `disable_clear_route_cache: true` with `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n2. Remove any explicit `disable_clear_route_cache: false` settings and use `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` instead\n3. Update any control plane configurations that generate ext_proc configs\n\n**Deprecation Timeline:**\n- v1.31.0: Both fields supported, both annotations present\n- v1.32.0+: Likely still supported, but planning should begin\n- Future: May be moved to oneof grouping or removed entirely\n\n---\n\n## 4. New Features\n\n### 4.1 Route Cache Action Enum\n\n**Status:** New - Stable and recommended\n\n**Proto Definition:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n\n    // Default behavior: clear route cache only when ext_proc response\n    // has clear_route_cache field set\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear the route cache when external processor responds\n    // with request headers, regardless of clear_route_cache setting\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Never clear the route cache, even if ext_proc sets clear_route_cache\n    // Equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache: true\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18;\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n\n**Case 1: Routes requiring fresh routing decisions**\n```yaml\n# Always recompute routes after ext_proc processing\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    route_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n**Case 2: Routes where auth decisions determine routing**\n```yaml\n# External processor makes auth decisions that affect routing\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Honor ext_proc's clear_route_cache\n```\n\n**Case 3: Read-only observation mode**\n```yaml\n# External processor only observes, never changes routes\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n### 4.2 Deferred Stream Closure Timeout\n\n**Status:** New - Specifically for observability_mode\n\n**Proto Definition:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Specifies the deferred closure timeout for gRPC stream\n  // that connects to external processor. Currently, the deferred\n  // stream closure is only used in observability_mode.\n  //\n  // In observability mode, gRPC streams may be held open to the\n  // external processor longer than the lifetime of the regular client\n  // to backend stream. Envoy will eventually timeout the external\n  // processor stream according to this time limit.\n  //\n  // Default: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n  google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n\n**Example: Extended observability window**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    observability_mode: true\n    # Keep the gRPC stream open for 30 seconds after the client disconnects\n    # to allow the external processor to continue observing\n    deferred_close_timeout: \"30s\"\n```\n\n**Important Notes:**\n- Only used when `observability_mode: true`\n- Default timeout is 5 seconds if not specified\n- The external processor can still close the stream before the timeout expires\n- This feature addresses flow control concerns and external processor buffering needs\n\n**Implementation:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.proto` (lines 260-265)\n\n### 4.3 Enhanced Error Handling\n\n**Status:** New - Minor behavioral change in error responses\n\nThe error handling for timeout scenarios has been improved to be more semantically correct.\n\n**Change:**\n- **v1.30.0:** Timeout errors return `500 Internal Server Error`\n- **v1.31.0:** Timeout errors return `504 Gateway Timeout`\n\n**Rationale:**\n- `504 Gateway Timeout` is semantically correct for upstream service timeouts\n- `500 Internal Server Error` incorrectly suggests an internal Envoy issue\n- This improves observability and makes client error handling more accurate\n\n**Affected Scenarios:**\n- External processor doesn't respond within `message_timeout`\n- External processor doesn't respond within `max_message_timeout`\n- In synchronous processing mode only (no timeout in async mode)\n\n**Configuration Example:**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext-proc-cluster\n    # Set appropriate timeouts\n    message_timeout: \"200ms\"  # Default\n    max_message_timeout: \"1000ms\"  # Optional\n```\n\n**Migration Impact:**\n- If downstream clients depend on receiving `500` for ext_proc failures, they may need adjustment\n- Monitoring and alerting rules looking for `500` errors will no longer catch ext_proc timeouts\n- Update log aggregation and APM tools to monitor `504` for ext_proc failures\n\n---\n\n## 5. Configuration Updates\n\n### 5.1 Required Configuration Changes\n\nNone. All v1.30.0 configurations remain valid and functional in v1.31.0.\n\n### 5.2 Recommended Configuration Updates\n\n#### Update 1: Migrate from `disable_clear_route_cache` to `route_cache_action`\n\n**Before:**\n```yaml\nfilters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext-proc-cluster\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**After:**\n```yaml\nfilters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext-proc-cluster\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n    # RECOMMENDED: Use explicit route cache action\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # or DEFAULT or CLEAR as appropriate\n```\n\n#### Update 2: Add Observability Mode Configuration (if using observability_mode)\n\n```yaml\nfilters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext-proc-cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n    # NEW: Control how long to keep the stream open for observations\n    deferred_close_timeout: \"5s\"  # 5 seconds (default)\n```\n\n### 5.3 Per-Route Configuration Updates\n\nNo changes required to per-route configurations. The `ExtProcPerRoute` and `ExtProcOverrides` messages remain unchanged.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Behavioral Changes\n\n### 6.1 Route Cache Action Default Behavior\n\n**Field:** `route_cache_action` (field 18)\n**Type:** `RouteCacheAction` enum\n**Default Value:** `DEFAULT` (0)\n\n**Behavior:**\n- When set to `DEFAULT`: The filter respects the `clear_route_cache` field in the external processor's response to request headers\n- When set to `CLEAR`: The filter always clears the route cache after external processing of request headers\n- When set to `RETAIN`: The filter never clears the route cache, even if the external processor requests it\n\n**Change from v1.30.0:**\n- v1.30.0 didn't have explicit CLEAR option; it was implicit in the default behavior\n- v1.30.0 had only two states via boolean: DEFAULT (route cache honored ext_proc) or RETAIN (never clear)\n\n### 6.2 Error Status Code Changes\n\n**Affected:** Timeout scenarios in ext_proc processing\n\n**Before (v1.30.0):**\n```\nHTTP/1.1 500 Internal Server Error\n```\n\n**After (v1.31.0):**\n```\nHTTP/1.1 504 Gateway Timeout\n```\n\n**When This Occurs:**\n- External processor doesn't respond before `message_timeout` expires\n- In synchronous processing mode (not observability_mode)\n- Only affects downstream error responses; upstream timeout handling unchanged\n\n**Impact Areas:**\n- Client-side error handling\n- Monitoring and alerting\n- Logs and tracing spans\n- Custom error pages/responses\n\n### 6.3 gRPC Tracing Context Propagation\n\n**Status:** Improved in v1.31.0\n\n**Change:** Tracing context headers are now properly propagated in bidirectional gRPC streams when using ext_proc.\n\n**Affected Clients:**\n- Envoy gRPC client (via `config.core.v3.GrpcService.envoy_grpc`)\n- Google C++ gRPC client (via `config.core.v3.GrpcService.google_grpc`)\n\n**Benefits:**\n- Distributed tracing works correctly with ext_proc\n- OpenTelemetry and Jaeger integrations improved\n- Better observability for ext_proc request/response timing\n\n**Configuration Impact:**\n- No changes needed; this works automatically\n- Tracing spans will now show correct parent-child relationships with ext_proc calls\n\n---\n\n## 7. Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Review Current Configuration\n\n```bash\n# Examine all ext_proc filter configurations\ngrep -r \"ext_proc\" /path/to/config\n\n# Check for uses of disable_clear_route_cache\ngrep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" /path/to/config\n```\n\n### Step 2: Plan Route Cache Migration\n\nFor each ext_proc filter configuration:\n\n| Current Setting | Migration Path | New Setting |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | Keep as-is or upgrade | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` | Keep as-is or upgrade | Remove field, use implicit DEFAULT |\n| Not specified (implicit DEFAULT) | Keep as-is or upgrade | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` |\n\n### Step 3: Update Monitoring and Alerting\n\nUpdate any monitoring rules that check for `500 Internal Server Error`:\n\n```yaml\n# OLD: Catch all 500 errors including ext_proc timeouts\n- alert: HighErrorRate\n  expr: rate(envoy_http_requests_total{response_code=\"500\"}[5m]) > 0.05\n\n# NEW: Separate concerns\n- alert: ExtProcTimeout\n  expr: rate(envoy_http_requests_total{response_code=\"504\"}[5m]) > 0.05\n- alert: OtherServerErrors\n  expr: rate(envoy_http_requests_total{response_code=\"500\"}[5m]) > 0.05\n```\n\n### Step 4: Update Logging and Analysis\n\nIf you have custom log parsing or analysis:\n\n```\n# v1.30.0 logs for ext_proc timeout\n[2024-04-15 10:23:45] ERROR ext_proc timeout -> HTTP 500\n\n# v1.31.0 logs for ext_proc timeout\n[2024-07-19 10:23:45] ERROR ext_proc timeout -> HTTP 504\n```\n\n### Step 5: Stage Deployment\n\n**Phase 1: Development/Staging**\n1. Deploy v1.31.0 Envoy binaries\n2. Keep all ext_proc configs unchanged (backward compatible)\n3. Verify ext_proc functionality with existing configs\n4. Test error handling with intentional timeouts\n\n**Phase 2: Production Canary**\n1. Route 5-10% of production traffic through v1.31.0\n2. Monitor error rates, latencies, and 504 vs 500 error distribution\n3. Verify that `504` errors are only ext_proc timeouts\n4. Validate downstream client error handling\n\n**Phase 3: Gradual Rollout**\n1. Gradually increase traffic through v1.31.0\n2. Update config for `route_cache_action` on non-critical routes\n3. Validate route caching behavior changes\n4. Monitor for any unexpected interactions\n\n**Phase 4: Update Configuration**\n1. Update all ext_proc configs to use `route_cache_action`\n2. Remove `disable_clear_route_cache` from configs\n3. Add `deferred_close_timeout` if using `observability_mode`\n4. Complete rollout to 100%\n\n### Step 6: Configuration Examples\n\n**Example 1: Basic Auth Service (DEFAULT route cache handling)**\n```yaml\n# Before\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: auth-processor\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n\n# After (optional, uses default behavior)\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: auth-processor\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n    route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n\n**Example 2: Read-Only Logging Service (RETAIN route cache)**\n```yaml\n# Before\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: log-processor\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true\n    observability_mode: true\n\n# After\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: log-processor\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN\n    observability_mode: true\n    deferred_close_timeout: \"5s\"\n```\n\n**Example 3: Authorization Service with Dynamic Routes (CLEAR route cache)**\n```yaml\n# NEW in v1.31.0 - Not possible in v1.30.0\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: auth-processor\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n    # Always recompute routes after auth decisions\n    route_cache_action: CLEAR\n    # Modify headers based on auth outcome\n    mutation_rules:\n      allow_all_headers: false\n      allow_envoy_headers: false\n      allowed_headers:\n        patterns:\n        - exact: \"x-user-id\"\n        - exact: \"x-user-role\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## 8. Testing Recommendations\n\n### 8.1 Unit Testing\n\n**Test Case 1: Route Cache Action Behavior**\n```go\n// Test DEFAULT: cache cleared only if ext_proc says so\nfunc TestRouteCacheActionDefault() {\n    // Configure route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n    // Send ext_proc response with clear_route_cache: true\n    // Assert: route cache was cleared\n\n    // Send ext_proc response with clear_route_cache: false\n    // Assert: route cache was NOT cleared\n}\n\n// Test CLEAR: cache always cleared\nfunc TestRouteCacheActionClear() {\n    // Configure route_cache_action: CLEAR\n    // Send ext_proc response with clear_route_cache: false\n    // Assert: route cache was cleared anyway\n}\n\n// Test RETAIN: cache never cleared\nfunc TestRouteCacheActionRetain() {\n    // Configure route_cache_action: RETAIN\n    // Send ext_proc response with clear_route_cache: true\n    // Assert: route cache was NOT cleared\n}\n```\n\n**Test Case 2: Error Status Codes**\n```go\nfunc TestExtProcTimeoutReturns504() {\n    // Configure message_timeout: 100ms\n    // Don't respond from ext_proc\n    // Assert: Returns HTTP 504\n    // Assert: NOT HTTP 500\n}\n```\n\n### 8.2 Integration Testing\n\n**Test Scenario 1: Backward Compatibility**\n```yaml\n# v1.30.0 config should work unchanged in v1.31.0\n---\napiVersion: v1\nkind: ConfigMap\nmetadata:\n  name: envoy-config-v130\ndata:\n  envoy.yaml: |\n    http_filters:\n    - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n      typed_config:\n        \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n        grpc_service:\n          envoy_grpc:\n            cluster_name: ext-proc\n        route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n### 8.3 Load Testing\n\n```bash\n# Load test with timeout scenarios\n# Verify 504 responses under load\n# Verify deferred_close_timeout behavior with observability_mode\n\nwrk -t12 -c400 -d30s http://envoy:10000/test \\\n  --latency\n\n# Check response codes\n# HTTP 504 should appear in timeout scenarios\n```\n\n### 8.4 End-to-End Testing\n\n**Test Checklist:**\n- [ ] Ext_proc filter loads without errors\n- [ ] Request headers are sent to external processor\n- [ ] Response headers are properly processed\n- [ ] Route cache is cleared/retained per configuration\n- [ ] Timeout returns 504 (not 500)\n- [ ] Observability mode works with deferred_close_timeout\n- [ ] Multiple ext_proc filters in chain work correctly\n- [ ] Per-route overrides still work\n- [ ] Failure mode allows gracefully handles processor errors\n- [ ] Tracing shows correct parent-child relationships\n\n---\n\n## 9. Rollback Guidance\n\n### 9.1 Quick Rollback Procedure\n\nIf issues are detected post-upgrade:\n\n**Step 1: Revert Envoy Binary**\n```bash\n# Stop v1.31.0 Envoy\nsystemctl stop envoy\n\n# Restore v1.30.0 Envoy binary\ncp /path/to/envoy-v1.30.0 /usr/local/bin/envoy\n\n# Restart with old binary\nsystemctl start envoy\n```\n\n**Step 2: Revert Configuration** (if you updated configs)\n```bash\n# Restore v1.30.0 configs from backup\ncp /backup/envoy-config-v1.30.0.yaml /etc/envoy/envoy.yaml\n\n# Reload configuration\nenvoy-cli config reload\n```\n\n**Step 3: Verify Rollback**\n```bash\n# Check version\nenvoy --version  # Should show 1.30.0\n\n# Verify traffic is flowing\ncurl http://envoy:10000/health  # Should return 200\n\n# Monitor error codes\n# Should NOT see 504 responses\n# Should see 500 for ext_proc timeouts again\n```\n\n### 9.2 Known Issues and Workarounds\n\n#### Issue: 504 errors breaking downstream error handling\n\n**Symptom:** Client applications expecting 500 errors are not handling 504 correctly\n\n**Workaround 1: Custom Error Handler**\n```lua\n-- Add a Lua filter to convert 504 \u2192 500 if needed\n-- This is NOT recommended, just for emergency rollback\nif response.status_code == 504 then\n  response.status_code = 500\nend\n```\n\n**Workaround 2: Update Client Applications**\n- Update error handling to treat 504 same as 500\n- This is the correct long-term solution\n\n#### Issue: Route cache not being cleared/retained as expected\n\n**Symptom:** Route decisions aren't being recomputed correctly\n\n**Troubleshooting:**\n1. Verify `route_cache_action` is set correctly\n2. Check ext_proc logs for `clear_route_cache` value\n3. Verify the external processor is configured correctly\n4. Check if routes are actually being matched (use `debug` log level)\n\n**Workaround:** Explicitly set route_cache_action matching your intent:\n```yaml\n# Ensure explicit behavior\nroute_cache_action: DEFAULT  # or CLEAR or RETAIN\n```\n\n### 9.3 Version-Specific Support\n\n**v1.30.0:**\n- Oldest supported configuration format\n- Uses `disable_clear_route_cache` (boolean)\n- Returns 500 for ext_proc timeouts\n- No `deferred_close_timeout` support\n\n**v1.31.0:**\n- Current version (this migration guide)\n- Supports both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`\n- Returns 504 for ext_proc timeouts\n- Supports `deferred_close_timeout`\n- Recommended migration target\n\n**v1.32.0+ (Future):**\n- Likely to deprecate `disable_clear_route_cache` further\n- Possible conversion to oneof fields\n- Monitor release notes for deprecation warnings\n\n---\n\n## 10. Compatibility Matrix\n\n### Supported Upgrade Paths\n\n| From Version | To Version | Compatibility | Config Changes |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| 1.30.0 | 1.31.0 | \u2705 Fully Compatible | Optional (backward compatible) |\n| 1.31.0 | 1.30.0 | \u26a0\ufe0f Requires rollback | Use `disable_clear_route_cache` instead of `route_cache_action` |\n\n### Configuration Compatibility\n\n| Feature | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | \u2705 Supported | \u2705 Supported (deprecated) |\n| `route_cache_action` | \u274c Not available | \u2705 Supported (recommended) |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | \u274c Not available | \u2705 Supported |\n| Error status 500 for timeout | \u2705 Default | \u274c Changed to 504 |\n| Error status 504 for timeout | \u274c Not used | \u2705 New default |\n| Tracing context in gRPC | \u26a0\ufe0f Not propagated | \u2705 Propagated |\n| `observability_mode` | \u2705 Supported | \u2705 Supported (improved) |\n\n---\n\n## 11. Performance Considerations\n\n### 11.1 Route Cache Behavior Impact\n\n**Potential Performance Changes:**\n\n- **CLEAR action:** May increase CPU usage due to frequent route recomputation\n  - Mitigated by: Route matching is optimized with trie structures\n  - Use case: Only when necessary for correctness\n\n- **RETAIN action:** May improve performance if routes are expensive to compute\n  - Ensure: External processor doesn't need to influence routing\n  - Trade-off: Less flexibility but faster path\n\n- **DEFAULT action:** Balanced approach, respects ext_proc decisions\n\n### 11.2 Deferred Close Timeout Impact\n\n- **Default 5s timeout:** Minimal overhead, suitable for most deployments\n- **Longer timeouts (10s+):** May hold more gRPC connections, slight memory increase\n- **Shorter timeouts (1s):** May result in premature stream closure if processor is slow\n- **Observability mode:** Adds minimal overhead when no processing is done\n\n### 11.3 Tracing Context Impact\n\n- **New in v1.31.0:** Minimal performance impact (header propagation)\n- **Benefit:** Improved observability for distributed tracing\n- **No tuning needed:** Works automatically\n\n---\n\n## 12. Common Migration Patterns\n\n### Pattern 1: Simple Authentication Service\n\n**Description:** External service that validates requests but doesn't modify routes\n\n```yaml\n# v1.30.0\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: auth-service\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n    # Implicit DEFAULT: honor ext_proc's clear_route_cache\n```\n\n**Migration:** No changes needed; works as-is in v1.31.0\n\n### Pattern 2: Header Augmentation Service\n\n**Description:** External service that adds/modifies headers but doesn't need route recomputation\n\n```yaml\n# v1.30.0\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: header-service\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**Migration:**\n```yaml\n# v1.31.0 - Recommended update\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: header-service\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Explicit intent: don't recompute routes\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: Logging/Observability Service\n\n**Description:** External service that only observes; no modification or routing changes\n\n```yaml\n# v1.30.0\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: logger\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n    observability_mode: true\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**Migration:**\n```yaml\n# v1.31.0 - Enhanced configuration\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: logger\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n    observability_mode: true\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN\n    # NEW: Control how long to keep stream for observations\n    deferred_close_timeout: \"10s\"  # Extended window for batch processing\n```\n\n### Pattern 4: Dynamic Routing Service\n\n**Description:** External service that makes routing decisions (NEW capability in v1.31.0)\n\n```yaml\n# v1.31.0 - Not possible in v1.30.0\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: routing-service\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n    # NEW: Always recompute routes after external processor\n    route_cache_action: CLEAR\n    # Processor can modify headers to affect routing\n    mutation_rules:\n      allow_all_headers: false\n      allowed_headers:\n        patterns:\n        - exact: \"x-routing-decision\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## 13. FAQ\n\n**Q: Do I need to upgrade immediately?**\nA: No. v1.31.0 is fully backward compatible with v1.30.0 configurations. Upgrade at your convenience, but take advantage of new features like `route_cache_action` for clarity.\n\n**Q: Will my ext_proc filter break after upgrade?**\nA: No. All v1.30.0 configurations continue to work exactly as before. The 504 error code change is the only behavioral difference, which is semantically more correct.\n\n**Q: Can I downgrade from v1.31.0 to v1.30.0?**\nA: Yes, but you must remove `route_cache_action` and `deferred_close_timeout` fields if used. The core ext_proc functionality is identical.\n\n**Q: Should I update `disable_clear_route_cache` to `route_cache_action`?**\nA: Yes, eventually. It makes intent clearer and prepares for potential future deprecation. But it's not urgent since both work in v1.31.0.\n\n**Q: What if my clients depend on receiving 500 errors?**\nA: Update your clients to handle 504 the same way. This is the correct HTTP semantics for upstream timeouts. 504 actually provides better debugging information.\n\n**Q: Does observability_mode work differently in v1.31.0?**\nA: No, functionally identical. But the new `deferred_close_timeout` field allows better control over stream lifetime for batched observations.\n\n**Q: Will there be a v1.31.1 or hotfixes?**\nA: Check the official Envoy release schedule. Bug fixes are typically released as patch versions (1.31.1, 1.31.2, etc.).\n\n**Q: What about the grpc tracing context propagation?**\nA: This is automatic in v1.31.0. If you use OpenTelemetry or Jaeger tracing, ext_proc calls will now appear correctly in traces. No configuration needed.\n\n---\n\n## 14.
